If so, it is puzzling: Since the murderer's stay in his city of refuge is to save him from the revenge of the avenger of blood (as is understood also from the beginning of the parsha, "And the cities shall be for you a refuge from the avenger, and the murderer shall not die")—why is the murderer's stay in the city of refuge extended for such a long time, "until the death of the Kohen Gadol"?

To resolve this question, Rashi brings two interpretations explaining that the obligation of his (extended) stay in the city of refuge is not (primarily) because of the fear of revenge from the avenger of blood, but rather this is (also, and primarily) a matter in its own right, imposed upon the murderer because of his act of murder. According to the first interpretation, it is because "it is not appropriate for him to be before the Kohen Gadol," and according to the second interpretation, it is because only then—at the death of the Kohen Gadol—is his sin atoned.

And that which is said here (at the beginning of the verse), "And the congregation shall save the murderer from the hand of the avenger of blood," does not mean that the fear is (only) lest the heart of the avenger of blood become hot and he kill him out of revenge—rather, the "rescue" is from a killing that is according to law, "he has no blood". That is to say: since if the murderer leaves his city of refuge and the avenger of blood finds him, the Torah says (as a continuation of the verses here), "and the avenger of blood kills the murderer, he has no blood"—it follows that his stay in his city of refuge is what saves him from being killed.

This is also the reason why in our parsha here, the verse states generally, "And the congregation shall save the murderer from the hand of the avenger of blood," and the verse does not explain—like in *Parshas Shoftim* —that this is because of the fear that "lest... his heart becomes hot" of the avenger. For in our parsha, it is not speaking (only) because of the fear of revenge, but because of the killing of the murderer according to law.

D. With this, several other differences between the two parshios of the city of refuge—our parsha and *Parshas Shoftim*—are explained:

In our parsha: (a) several verses come first regarding one who kills a person intentionally (which seemingly has no place here); (b) the time the murderer is obligated to remain in the city of refuge is stated—"until the death of the Kohen Gadol"; (c) the law is stated afterward for when the murderer leaves his city of refuge (after having come there) and the avenger of blood kills him; (d) the reason the avenger of blood is not liable for killing him is because "he has no blood" (as Rashi explains, "he is like one who kills the dead").

Whereas in *Parshas Shoftim*: (a) laws are given regarding preparing the way to the city of refuge ; (b) the law is given if the avenger of blood pursues the murderer on his way to the city of refuge ; (c) and regarding this it is said that "he (the murderer) has no judgment of death, for he was not an enemy to him from yesterday or the day before."

Based on the above, the reason for the differences is understood:

In *Parshas Shoftim*, it speaks about saving the murderer from the revenge of the avenger of blood, a fear that is (primarily) only immediate, at the time of fleeing to the city of refuge. Therefore, the laws of preparing the way to the city of refuge (and also to prepare "many cities of refuge") were stated there, so that the murderer could flee there—"lest the avenger of blood pursue the murderer because his heart is hot, and overtake him because the way is long..." For then there is the fear that "lest he pursue... because his heart is hot" (and in this, the verse emphasizes that "he has no judgment of death" to be killed by the avenger of blood when he is still on his way to the city of refuge).

This is not the case in our parsha, which speaks (primarily) about the (continued) stay of the murderer in his city of refuge after the fear of the avenger of blood's revenge has already ceased. The rescue of the city of refuge is so that the avenger of blood will not kill him according to law.

Therefore, the verse precedes this with the laws of one who kills a person intentionally, and emphasizes (twice) "the avenger of blood shall kill the murderer when he meets him," meaning that the avenger of blood has an obligation from the Torah to kill the murderer. In continuation of this, it is said that for one who kills a person unintentionally, "the congregation shall judge between the striker and the avenger of blood according to these judgments. And the congregation shall save the murderer from the hand of the avenger of blood... and he shall dwell in it until the death of the Kohen Gadol... and if he leaves... and the avenger of blood finds him... and the avenger of blood kills the murderer, he has no blood." From this it is understood that these matters are laws of the Torah—that the judge forbids the avenger of blood from killing the murderer when he is in his city of refuge, and "if he leaves... the murderer leaves the border of his city of refuge... and the avenger of blood finds him... (the judgment is rendered that) the avenger of blood kills the murderer." The reason for this is because outside his city of refuge "he has no blood," "he is like one who kills the dead" (as above), because in this state, his judgment for death has been rendered.

E. Based on the above, the difference between the two interpretations of Rashi is understood, as is the reason Rashi needed to bring the second interpretation:

According to the first interpretation, that "he comes to cause... and the murderer comes to remove... it is not appropriate for him to be before the Kohen Gadol," it follows that the murderer's stay in his city of refuge is not a punishment and atonement for his sin, but a secondary matter connected to the Kohen Gadol, where the murderer brought himself into such a state that forces him to be not before the Kohen Gadol ("it is not appropriate for him to be before the Kohen Gadol").

But this interpretation is difficult (somewhat), for why would the murderer's leaving the city of refuge be so severe that "he has no blood" ("he is like the dead")—is it because he places himself in a state where "it is not appropriate (for him to be before the Kohen Gadol)" that a death penalty is imposed upon him ?

Furthermore: according to this, it follows that the fact that the city of refuge is a protection and rescue ("refuge") from the hand of the avenger of blood is a result and consequence of (the obligation to sit in this city and) the prohibition to leave it. For when he violates this prohibition, his blood is then permitted for death at the hand of the avenger of blood (as above at the end of the section)—which is the opposite of the simple meaning of the matter, that the cause (and beginning) of the obligation to place the murderer in this city is (because it is a "refuge," meaning) to save him "from the hand of the avenger of blood."

Therefore, Rashi brings a second interpretation, that until the death of the Kohen Gadol, his sin has not yet been atoned. Based on this, the reason is understood that if he leaves his city of refuge, "he has no blood," because until the death of the Kohen Gadol, he still has a death penalty upon him because of his act of murder, except that as long as he is in his city of refuge, it protects and saves him from this punishment.

F. From all of this, one can learn a wonderful lesson regarding the matter of the love and unity of Yisrael:

The Kohen Gadol is the highest level in the people of Yisrael, and one who kills a person unintentionally is the lowest level [for one who kills a person intentionally, his punishment is death and he is a dead man; but among those who remain alive, there is none lower than one who kills a person unintentionally, which is why only for him do we find the punishment of exile].

The verse teaches us that even they (the two extremes among Bnei Yisrael) are dependent upon one another, to the point that the Torah has linked the atonement of this person who killed a person unintentionally with the Kohen Gadol. For this is the essence of the Kohen Gadol—a lover of Yisrael, as we find regarding Aharon the Kohen Gadol, who was "a lover (even) of the creatures."

This is also the connection between the two interpretations of Rashi—that in both of them, the greatness of the Kohen Gadol's love for Yisrael is emphasized: in the first interpretation—on the side of the positive, that "he comes... to lengthen the days" of Yisrael [and as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains that this is the reason the chamber of the Kohen Gadol is called the "Chamber of Wood", for "wood indicates long life... 'as the days of the tree shall be the days of My people,'" and "the Kohen Gadol is connected to long life, as it is written 'length of days is in its right hand,' so long life is drawn from the aspect of the right, which is kindness... and this is the aspect of the Kohen Gadol"];

And afterward, Rashi adds even more, that the Kohen Gadol involves himself even in the welfare of such people who need to be prayed for so that a mishap will not occur through them to Yisrael—he prays for them as well, and his prayer is accepted so that there will be only good and kindness for Yisrael, always, all the days.

(From a Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Matos-Masei, 5734)


## במדבר 

## 215

### Bamidbar

...Regarding what you wrote about the explanation in Likutei Torah, Bamidbar (15d), that there are four senses and not five — if we assume there is no typographical error here, it can be explained by the fact that he emphasizes here the *hislabshus* (enclothement) according to the temperament and nature, which is not the case with the sense of touch (see the explanation of foreign terms in Moreh Nevuchim, end of Part I, entry "Sense." See also the note from Ra'aya Mehemna — Zohar Vol. III, 229b — and its commentaries there). . .
[quotation](From a letter dated 29 Sivan, 5720)[/quotation]


## ר"ח סיון

## 216

### Rosh Chodesh Sivan

By the grace of Hashem, Sunday, Parshas Naso, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5749, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

"In the third month after the children of Israel had gone forth from the land of Egypt, on this day"—this refers to Rosh Chodesh—"they came to the wilderness of Sinai. And Israel encamped there"—using the singular form, "like one man with one heart"—"opposite the mountain," to receive the Torah from Mount Sinai.

And on the second day, it was said to them, "And you shall be for Me"—a term denoting both a command and a promise—"a kingdom of priests."

## 222

There was a revelation among them of the attribute of *ahavas Yisrael*, reaching the level of unity among the Jewish people. According to the words of our Sages, this was the *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below) for the Holy One, Blessed be He, to decide to give the Torah to the people of Israel.

And since "these days are remembered and observed" every single year, the time is auspicious for every man and woman to be aroused and to strengthen themselves in all of the above.

A further lesson from all this is based on the well-known saying of the Alter Rebbe at the beginning of our Parsha: "When you kindle the lamps"—which refers to the "lamp of Hashem, the soul of man," in such a way that "the flame rises by itself"—a continuous, ongoing action, and so on.

This has a special relevance for students, as they must be lamps that illuminate—themselves, their homes, their surroundings, and the entire world—with the "lamp of mitzvah and the light of Torah," and with the "light of the Torah," which is the inner dimension of Torah, through the dissemination of which the King Moshiach will come.

May it be fulfilled immediately: "Gladden the soul of Your servant... turn to me and be gracious to me; grant Your strength to Your servant and save," with the true and complete Redemption.

With blessings for success in all the above.

## 223

...May it be the will of Hashem that these auspicious days, regarding which it is said "And Israel encamped" in the singular form, as our Sages expounded, should also influence [the recipients]—and especially [regarding] the aforementioned—that they should all become one group, with one opinion, and as one man, to fulfill our task in this world. For man was created to serve his Creator, which in our current era means the dissemination of the wellsprings [outward] (until they reach) the outermost reaches, and specifically through love. As is explained in many places, since the exile [is] due to the sin of baseless hatred, the rectification must necessarily be the exact opposite. And this is understood.

It is understood that my intention in these lines is not only for him, but for each and every one. May Hashem grant him merit and success to bring good tidings regarding all that has been said.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good tidings in all the above.

(From a letter dated 27 Iyar 5716)


## ימי הגבלה

## 224

### Days of Preparation (Yimei Hagbalah)

**From the Sicha of the first day of Yimei Hagbalah**
**— Night of 3 Sivan, eve of Wednesday, Parshas Nasso, 5749**

1. Today marks the beginning of the three days of preparation (*Yimei Hagbalah*) for the time of the giving of our Torah, when Moshe instructed the Jewish people (on the third of Sivan) regarding the "mitzvah of limitation" (*mitzas hagbalah*): "And you shall set bounds for the people round about, saying, 'Take heed to yourselves, that you go not up into the mount, or touch the border of it...'" and "Set bounds about the mount, and sanctify it."

The simple reason for the command, "Set bounds about the mount, and sanctify it," is due to the holiness of the mountain; therefore, the Jewish people had to be careful not to even touch it.

When one contemplates this more deeply, it is reasonable to say that this is also a preparation and introduction to the giving of the Torah. Especially since Hashem commanded this with a detailed elaboration, and did so twice—once at the beginning of the three days, and again on the third day: "Warn the people, lest they break through to Hashem to gaze... go down... and warn them a second time."

2. The explanation for this is as follows:
The intention of the giving of the Torah is the giving of the Torah specifically *below*, in this physical world. On the contrary, "It is not in heaven" (to the point that Hashem promises the heavenly Beis Din, "I and you shall go to the Beis Din below..." to hear how they rule the law).

This is also the ultimate purpose and intent of man’s *avodah* (as it was uniquely established at the giving of the Torah)—not as it was with the sons of Aharon, who, due to their intense *teshukah* to draw close to Hashem, expired in *kallos hanefesh* ("when they drew near before Hashem and died"). In the words of the Ohr HaChaim HaKadosh: "They did not refrain from drawing near to the pleasant, sweet, friendly, and beloved closeness, the kisses of sweetness, until their souls expired from them."

Rather, the *avodah* must specifically be that of *neshamos* in *gufim* (souls within bodies). It must be with the full fire and passion to be close to Hashem, but simultaneously, it must be in a manner of "the bush was not consumed"—as was the case with Rabbi Akiva, who "entered in peace and departed in peace." (To the extent that his entry was different—specifically *in peace*, in such a way and with the intention that there would subsequently be a departure in peace and wholeness, a soul within a body). That is to say, both things must exist: "entered," and together with that, "in peace"—in a manner and with the intention of "departing in peace." And furthermore: specifically through this "departing in peace" does one become a true and complete *keli* for the highest revelations (for the sake of which he "entered").

[This is also hinted at in what Hashem commanded during the days of preparation (on the second day) for the giving of the Torah (even before the command of "And you shall set bounds..."): "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation." Together with the fact that Jews are a "kingdom of priests," which indicates their separation from the world—just as a *kohein* "who was set apart to serve Hashem, to minister to Him," and especially a *Kohein Gadol*, whose place is specifically in Jerusalem (complete *yirah*, and "a city that is joined together," not divided among the tribes, for he is above division) and he must not leave that place—they, the Jewish people, must also be a "holy nation." As they find themselves as a "nation" in this physical world, *neshamos* in *gufim*, they must be "holy," holy and separated. This is similar to what is explained in *Torah Or* (at the beginning) and *Ohr HaTorah* (in the annotations on *Torah Or*) regarding the concept of "charity exalts a nation," that as Jews stand at the level of "nation," where they must attain an elevation, a state of "exaltation" is generated within them.]

It can be said that this is one of the reasons why, before the giving of the Torah, there was the decree that "the higher realms shall not descend below, and the lower realms shall not ascend above"—even though the intention (at the beginning of creation and within it) was for both: Torah and Israel, leading to the unification of the higher and lower realms. The intention is that the lower realms should remain in their existence (not be nullified to the higher realms). For this reason, Hashem created the lower realms in such a way that, initially, there is a decree (also from the word *ligzor*—to cut)—a separation and detachment between the higher and lower realms. Through this, the lower realms can remain in their existence. This achieves that later, when the decree is nullified (at the time of the giving of the Torah)—when one receives the power to draw down both higher and lower realms—it should be in a way that the lower realms do not lose their existence (and become nullified to the higher), but rather, as they are an existence of the lower realms, they become a *keli* for the higher realms. In other words: the physicality of the world becomes an object of *kedushah*.

Therefore, as an introduction and preparation for the giving of the Torah, there had to be the safeguard and caution of "And you shall set bounds...":

After the great elevation that the Jewish people reached on Rosh Chodesh Sivan, "on this day," when "they came to the wilderness of Sinai," and "Israel encamped there before the mountain," "as one man with one heart," through which the Jewish people became worthy of receiving the Torah [in the words of the Midrash: "When they came to Sinai, they encamped in one encampment... Hashem said, 'Since they love peace and have become one encampment, this is the time for Me to give them My Torah'"]—after their longing for the giving of the Torah throughout the forty-nine days preceding it (which the Jewish people counted due to their yearning for the giving of the Torah)—their *hispaalus* and fire (standing by Har Sinai) could have led them to want to ascend the mountain and be with Hashem, in the words of Rashi: "Their desire was toward Hashem, to gaze, and they drew near to the side of the mountain."

Therefore, Hashem warned, "Take heed to yourselves, that you go not up into the mount, or touch the border of it," "Set bounds about the mount, and sanctify it"—so that they would not expire and be nullified through their tremendous *teshukah* and fire while standing by Har Sinai ("before the mountain"), which had (also) effected an elevation in them (after Rosh Chodesh Sivan). Rather, their *ta'avah* and *teshukah* should be connected with their existence as *neshamos* in *gufim* (who are together receiving the Torah). Therefore, Hashem commanded, "And you shall set bounds... Take heed to yourselves, that you go not up into the mount, or touch the border of it"—not only should they not ascend the mountain (similar to the ascent and *kallos hanefesh* of the sons of Aharon), but they should not even "touch the border of it."

3. "And these days are remembered and kept" every year as new, until they are truly new:
At the time of the giving of our Torah each year, a novelty occurs in the completeness of the nullification of the decree, and specifically the connection of the higher and lower realms. In relation to this novelty and completeness, the nullification of the decree in previous years is like the state before the nullification of the decree; there is still the distinction and lack of unification between the higher and lower realms.

Therefore, in the days of preparation for the time of the giving of our Torah, both matters are required: the drawing near to stand "before the mountain," and the "Israel encamped there," as one man with one heart, with the great *hishtokekus* for the receiving of the Torah; and together with this—"And you shall set bounds," so that one can receive the Torah in its completeness, as *neshamos* in *gufim*, both healthy, for long life and good years, so that it will be a case of "(entered in peace and) departed in peace."

4. It should be added—based on the setting of Rosh Chodesh Sivan this year—on the first day of the week:
Every Sunday is analogous to the (first) Sunday of the work of creation, which is called "one day," "on which Hashem was unique in His world, for there was no one in His world but Him."

Also, the creation that occurred on the first day was—light, which is generally higher than the (rest of the) creation, and certainly the light created on the first day, which the world was not worthy to use (and therefore, "Hashem hid it for the *tzaddikim* in the future to come").

[And even the level of light that shines now is higher than the rest of the creation. As is known and understood, the superiority of light comes from the fact that hearing is not like seeing. Through seeing (by means of light), one perceives immediately, in a single glance, the entire matter with all its details. On the contrary—the details stand in a single existence, which is above division, and only afterwards is this drawn down from the general to the particular. Whereas through hearing, it is the opposite: first one hears one detail and then another, etc., and from the details one arrives at the general, until one assembles the picture of the entire matter.]

It can be said that this corresponds to the fact that on Rosh Chodesh Sivan (the first of Sivan)—on the Sunday of this year (of the Sicha)—there was the concept of "encamped" (*vayichan*), in the singular, "as one man with one heart" (similar to the concept of "one day," "light" (day), which is (by nature) above division).

The intention, however, is that afterwards, the revelation of "unique" and "one" should descend into the particulars, into the boundaries of the division of creation (the lower realms).

Therefore, there follows on the third day (3 Sivan) the command of "And you shall set bounds... Take heed to yourselves, that you go not up into the mount, or touch the border of it."

But specifically through this limitation, the Jewish people are prepared for the giving of the Torah, the completeness of the connection between the higher and lower realms, and the unification of the Jewish people with Hashem—


## חג השבועות

## 231

### Shavuos

Regarding the matter of not reciting *Akdamus* — it is a great wonder, given that he is in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established. Apparently, he was not aware that among all the Sephardim, the aforementioned custom does not exist, and even in Lubavitch they were not accustomed to reciting them (although I have not heard a reason for this; see *Sukkah* 44b, that since it has gone forth from his mouth, etc., they were careful to observe it even for the lenient side, see there).
(From a letter, 26 Sivan, 5719)

If you wish to say it as a *dvar malchus* (a witty insight):
One can connect the essence of *Matan Torah* with *shechitah* based on one of the reasons for eating dairy foods on Shavuos: that at the giving of the Torah, they were commanded regarding *shechitah*, and all agree that the Torah was given on Shabbos, and one does not slaughter on Shabbos; thus, they were compelled to eat dairy foods, as is brought in the *sefarim*.
And although, seemingly, they were accustomed to *shechitah* even before this, as our Sages of blessed memory said regarding the verse, "And slaughter a slaughtering and prepare" (*Chullin* 91a; and in the *Midrash* brought in *Tzror HaMor*, which notes the five laws of *shechitah*), it is understood simply that the Jewish people before receiving the Torah were not in the category of *bar zevichah* (subject to the laws of slaughter) as they were after *Matan Torah*.
(From a letter, 24 Iyar, 5721)

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of the 20th, as well as the book *Nuclear War and Nuclear Peace* by Yehoshafat Harkabi. Thank you for the past and also for the future, as you will surely continue in such matters.
As is the custom of the Jewish people to find hints in the Torah for every matter and detail, and as we stand a few days before the time of the giving of our Torah, the essence of Torah is to refine the material and the physical until the powers hidden within them are revealed, and until the first source—the power of the Actor in the acted-upon—is reached, through whose word the heavens were made and by the breath of His mouth all their host. From this, it is understood how great are the powers that exist in every thing and matter; one only needs to penetrate to the interior of the material to reveal, as mentioned, that which is hidden within its very core and interior.

## 232

And now, science is beginning to discover this in matter in the literal sense, which is one of the points of investigation in the field of nuclear science. And from level to level and from degree to degree, the investigation deepens also regarding human beings and their affairs, for in the style of our Sages of blessed memory, each one is an entire world. And especially if one makes the interiority rule over the exteriority, the form over the matter, and the true spirituality over the garments and *kelipos* that cover it, until every detail in creation—and all the more so the entirety of creation—will proclaim, "I am Hashem your G-d," "Hashem is the G-d, there is none else besides Him."
With respect and with blessings for *Moadim L'Simcha* and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with interiority.
(From a letter, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5724)

The annual luncheon (11 Sivan, G-d willing) is taking place this year in the days that are still connected to the *Yom Tov* of Shavuos, and surely all participants will stand under the fresh impression of the time of the giving of our Torah.
Jewish women have especially much to draw from the influence of the *Yom Tov* of *Kabbalas HaTorah*. For, as is known, the women were the first to whom the Almighty offered the holy Torah, and they accepted the Torah immediately, as our Sages of blessed memory explain the words: "Thus shall you say to the House of Jacob"—these are the women—"and tell the Children of Israel"—these are the men. And this underscores the great *zechus* of Jewish women—and together with it, also their great responsibility—for Torah and *mitzvos*.
And although every year all the matters of the *Yom Tov* are repeated, this itself is an indication that the connection to Torah and *mitzvos* must be renewed and refreshed to a stronger degree from year to year, especially taking into account that human powers also rise from year to year.
It is therefore quite understandable that your important work to support the holy *mosdos haTorah* of Lubavitch must be strengthened and expanded from year to year, especially since the *mosdos haTorah* themselves are constantly rising and are in need of increased help more and more.
May the Almighty grant that the annual undertaking should be with great success and should bring about a strengthened revival in your work, in quantity and in quality, and in the *zechus* of this, may you all, with your households...

## 234

Taking into account the above, I am confident that all those participating in the annual celebration will show special interest and dedication to enable this educational institution to strengthen and expand its important activities in education.
And surely the Almighty will bless and grant success to each and every one of the participants and supporters of the institution, within the entirety of the Jewish people, in all that is needed, in material and in spiritual matters alike.
With respect and with a blessing for success, for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with interiority.
(From a letter, Lag B'Omer, 5750)

Your letter reached me and caused me great pleasure. May the Almighty fulfill your hearts' desires for the good, to succeed in the study of Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim* (the Torah of life), for it is a guide in daily life and the source of blessing for a life that is truly good.
Surely you know about the *Yom Tov* of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, and you have also heard that the Torah was given only after all of Israel said, "Our children (including our daughters) are our guarantors." This means that in the *zechus* of the sons and daughters of Israel, the Torah was given to all of Israel. From this, it is understood how important it is for the children of Israel to conduct themselves according to the *mitzvos* and instructions of the Torah, and first and foremost in honoring parents and teachers and in diligence and perseverance in studies. And I hope that each one of you will be a living example of a daughter of Israel, a daughter of our matriarchs Sarah, Rebecca, Rachel, and Leah.
With a blessing for success and for good tidings.
(From a letter, 3 Sivan, 5765)

...And may it be the will that in these days before the giving of our Torah, regarding which it is told in *Shemos Rabbah* that all of Israel were healed in all matters and were healthy and whole for the receiving of the Torah, may this be fulfilled according to the interpretation of the Arizal on the verse, "And these days are remembered and performed"—may this be fulfilled in each one of us in its entirety,

## 235

and consequently, all the conflicts, etc., detailed above will disappear, and we will merit to receive the Torah with joy and with interiority and to continue its instructions for the entire year...
(From a letter, 2 Sivan, 5715)

...And since you wrote your letter at the conclusion of the *tashlumin* (completion) of *Matan Torah*, which brings healing to the world, and the Torah is a *Toras Chesed* (Torah of kindness) and "it is not in heaven" but specifically in this world, may you bring good news in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.
(From a letter, 16 Sivan, 5719)

...At its beginning. The Rambam's introduction. "All the *mitzvos*, etc., were given with their explanation, as it is said, 'And I will give you, etc.'—Torah is the Written Torah, and the *mitzvah* is its explanation, etc.—the Oral Torah." Seemingly, this requires study, for that the *mitzvos* were given with their explanation we derive from what is stated regarding *Shemitah*, "And He spoke, etc., at Mount Sinai," as it is in *Toras Kohanim* there. And it is even more difficult, for the Rambam himself brought this derivation regarding this matter in his introduction to the *Mishnah*.
Perhaps it can be explained according to what is known in the rules of the Rambam, that "it is his way to take the simplest *drashah*, etc., and sometimes he brings a verse not mentioned in the *Gemara* at all" (*Yad Malachi*, rules of the Rambam, and references there). And according to this, the precision of the *Tzofnas Paneach* on the Rambam (by the Rogatchover) is also resolved, for in the *Shas* (*Berachos* 5a) it explains, "the *mitzvah*—this is the *Mishnah*, etc., to teach them—this is the *Gemara*." And it is understood.
However, it is still difficult, for according to the Rambam we learn only that the *mitzvos* and their explanation were given to Moshe at Sinai, and from where do we know that also the *divrei sofrim*, etc., and everything that a veteran student is destined to innovate was given to Moshe at Sinai? And perhaps it can be said that he follows his own system, that all the decrees, enactments, and customs, etc., are a *mitzvah asei* to listen to them, etc. (*Hilchos Mamrim*, at its beginning)—and if so, the explanation of this *mitzvah asei* includes *divrei sofrim*, etc.
By the way: The Rambam's introduction to the *Mishnah*, *Seder Zeraim*—although it is printed as such in the *Shas*, etc.—it is proven from its content that it is not dedicated at all to *Seder Zeraim*, but rather to the entire *Shas*...
(From a letter, 10 Iyar, 5724)

## 238

...religion, interpretations, and explanations, etc., from which the conclusion is that although for several reasons it is necessary to bring what is found in the *Piskei Dinim* of the *Yad HaChazakah*, that the explanations in the Torah there are also a decided and absolute *halachah*, first and foremost there is room to quote from his book *Moreh Nevuchim*, his letters, and his commentary on the *Mishnah*. And it is understood.
(From a letter, 22 Adar, 5724)

...I read with interest about his relatives who are there, etc. And from one matter to another in the same matter, I will permit myself to copy here one of the points of what was spoken about in this matter, based on the *psak din* that all of Israel are one complete stature. And like the body, where the strengthening of health in any limb adds to the health of all the other limbs, so it is regarding the limbs of the individual complete stature mentioned. And from this, the immediate conclusion is that an addition in Torah and its *mitzvos* in action is the main thing—the fulfillment of practical *mitzvos* day by day, which are vital and the existence and foundation of all the children of Israel [fitting their name *Toras Chaim* and its *mitzvos*, of which it is said, "And he shall live by them"]. Surely, this adds to the "health" of each and every one of the children of Israel, and the place does not separate at all, and as mentioned, this is a certain and tangible help from the *mitzvah* itself, and also for the success of the efforts in other ways. And specifically regarding this help, no one is busy with it, and not even speaking of it. And *d'l* (a word to the wise).
And in this assistance, one does not need meetings and votes and asking the opinion of the majority, since each one has free choice in this and can add more and more, including also in influencing the other to bring him closer and closer to Torah and *mitzvos*, and through this to help all the children of Israel wherever they are, both in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and in the Diaspora, for they are all in need of help, even if not in the same area and to the same extent. And it is understood.
And the days are days of *segulah*, the days of *Sefirah* that connect the matter of the time of our freedom with the days of the receiving of the Torah, and with the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear," an acceptance together with a promise engraved on the tablets.
(From a letter, 23 Iyar, 5724)

In response to your letter in the name of the Herut Movement Center—an invitation to participate in the seventh national convention of the movement,
Together with my thanks for the honor and their desired thought,
In principle, it is impossible for me to do so. For one of the foundations of the Chabad-Lubavitch system

## 239

is not to identify with any party whatsoever, and therefore also not to participate in party conventions.
On this occasion, it is my duty to give expression to the deep and growing sorrow when observing the internal enslavement of certain circles of our people, the children of Israel—enslavement to the culture of the nations of the lands, the imitation of their way of life and their worldview, etc.—which is the known method of "let us be like the nations, like the families of the lands"—than which there is no greater exile and slavery.
And to express my hope that it may be the will that the convention will dedicate its best time and powers to publicize and instill the fundamental idea that there cannot be freedom as long as one is not absolutely freed from the aforementioned enslavement.
And from the line of negation to the line of affirmation—to publicize and instill the fundamental idea that the freedom of our people, the children of Israel, is only when it is "engraved on the tablets" (*charut al ha-luchot*), freedom founded on the service of G-d as it was engraved and explained on the tablets in the Torah of Hashem and His *mitzvos*.
Holy Torah—which is the testimony to a holy nation to whom the Holy Land was given, from the river of Egypt to the great river, the river Euphrates.
(From a letter, 18 Teves, 5763)

Thank you for the *pidyon nefesh* that I received through you... and especially for his attentiveness in conveying to me the content and the conclusion of his speech at the large assembly with the participation of the youth, which he concluded with the call of the prophet: "Return, O Israel... and I will return to you, says Hashem of Hosts."
It is understood that regarding such a thing there is no place to say thank you, for the reward of a *mitzvah* is a *mitzvah*. And in our days and in this period, there is here more than a *mitzvah*, if it is possible to say so. For the youth is the continuation of our generation in the present and the continuation of all the generations that preceded us. And in order for it to be a continuation, it is necessary that it be connected to the general continuation, to continue the eternal values of our people from the day it became a nation at the standing at Mount Sinai. And as it was then at the beginning of our becoming a nation, that the beginning and the foundation was—"I am Hashem your G-d who brought you out of the land of Egypt, from the house of slaves," which means that there cannot be true redemption from the house of slaves unless it is connected with "Hashem your G-d" and the rest of the commandments that follow this, both between man and G-d and between man and his fellow, which also cannot have existence unless they begin and are founded on "I am" and "You shall have no other," as we have witnessed clearly, especially in our generation, that when this foundation was missing, all the systems of ethics and philosophy, etc., did not help; and so it is also now.
And knowing you and that you are a man of action, I am confident that what you said to the youth will not remain only

## 240

as a matter of instruction on the path and the direction, but you will continue in this and activate all those over whom your influence extends and who listen to your voice, and in every place where your word reaches, and especially since our brethren, the children of Israel, in general, are a people of action, that the call "Return, O Israel and I will return to you" will not remain in the category of "the Merciful One desires the heart," but will find its proper expression in actual deed, and even to daily life itself...
(From a letter, 2 Kislev, 5763)

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 1st of Rosh Chodesh Elul and the one preceding it, and you have already been answered officially regarding the proposal about participating in the general poll, which is not the custom at all. And in any case, thank you for your attention.
I must add—and not as an addition, but that in truth this is the main point of my letter—that I had a great disappointment when reading your first letter. My intention:
Since the time of our conversation when you visited New York (which I hope you remember, at least its main points), I have followed and inquired and investigated if there are any results from the conversation. For our conversation, at least according to my intention, was not official and also not in the nature of an interview, but rather (as I think I also said explicitly) out of the recognition that exceptional ability and possibility stand at your disposal. And on the other hand, this period of ours, and especially the most recent years, is rich in possibilities beyond compare—possibilities regarding the strengthening and establishing of the position of our people, the children of Israel, wherever they are, and especially in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days by *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*.
Therefore, the demand of the hour is that whoever can do something in the aforementioned direction, it is his primary duty and his first task, and especially since this is for the benefit of the many and often also for the saving of the many.
The words are said even if the ability and possibility are in the category of doubt; all the more so when the past has proven that there are special powers and possibilities for a certain person to utilize them in the aforementioned direction, for then all the matters are with greater intensity and greater strength.
—And I will repeat, at least briefly, what we spoke about in our conversation:
Experience has proven that certain circles of our people are susceptible to influence, and especially the youth and the young people, who in the near future will direct the course of events in the settlements of the children of Israel, including in our Holy Land.
For several reasons, daily life has dissipated the enthusiasm of the youth and the young people,

## 241

and as a result of this, the activity in the desired direction. And this led to their energy being activated in undesirable directions and even to the opposite of what is desired. And the justification is that such-and-such a thing is boring and such-and-such an activity is old and ancient and its place was in past generations, etc., etc.
And it was my proposal that you utilize the energy and enthusiasm, which although a layer of the worry of daily life—ordinary life, i.e., gray—has covered over them, my hope is strong that you will awaken them and bring them to action, to ignite the youth and to enflame the spark hidden within them for positive actions that are a necessity for the life of the collective and also for the benefit of the individual.
However, during the years that have passed since our conversation, there has not come to my attention any actual deed as a result of my aforementioned words. My intention is simple: that despite my searching, I did not find in those journals in which you write, nor in other places that came to my sight, an echo of your activities in the aforementioned direction.
Seemingly, one could excuse the matter that you do not agree with my opinion. But the necessity to extract the youth and the young people from the lethargy is so clear and simple, and the lack of individuals who have prospects of succeeding in this is so great, that in my opinion it is impossible that there should be any doubt in this matter of the command of the hour, especially regarding each and every one who has succeeded in the past in this area.
Surely there is benefit in meetings with people who occupy a leading place in various circles, to know their opinion and to publicize it, etc., etc., and since you are busy with this, you surely see this benefit tangibly, but this does not exempt at all from a direct meeting with the active part of every people, and so too in the people of the children of Israel, a part whose measure of energy is greater than in the other parts of the people, that part which has not yet been affected by a life of compromise for decades of years until it became its second nature, that part which is not afraid of a challenge and has the courage of spirit to admit it if it finds that its path in life was not in order and to begin a new way of life, in a new direction, and sometimes also the opposite, from the direction of its life before then—that all these qualities will not be found in party leaders and also not in most leaders of any circle whatsoever.
It is understood that after a few months had passed since our conversation and I did not see any action and results from it, I looked for an excuse and reason to write to you and to ask you about the aforementioned, but for several reasons the matter was delayed from time to time. And one of the main reasons was that I did not know what your reaction would be, that on the basis of one conversation and one meeting I would express an opinion regarding "your life," and especially an opinion that demands a change in your activities and a fundamental change. And another reason, more internal, and perhaps also more fundamental, the health of the child, etc., that you told me about (in addition to what I heard from the side). And sorrow prevents a person from several matters, and especially matters that demand more energy and a war to a significant extent against the current, which causes loneliness, etc.
My disappointment that I could not reach you and move you to the actions about which we spoke grew even more in the period close to the Six Day War and these days themselves and the days that followed them, that during this time the enthusiasm of all circles of our people was at its peak everywhere, and there was missing

## 242

completely a direction toward a positive goal and a positive matter of building in spirituality and in physicality. And to our great sorrow, the people did not find the leaders who would guide it and direct its enthusiasm toward positive actions, and not even those who would strengthen the enthusiasm and encourage it, and also in this period the matters go and "arrange themselves" in the known formula, that they move on to the order of the day. And also in these days I did not find a trace of your activities.
It is simple that what is written above is not in the nature of preaching morality, G-d forbid, but rather an attempt once again to renew a conversation, even if in writing, in the content of our first conversation, etc., and perhaps now your activities will come in the aforementioned direction. And in a concrete way: to elevate the youth and the young people to the eternal essence of our people, which together with the eternity of the matters are, in the style of our Sages of blessed memory, new every day.
And for example: propaganda for internal *aliyah*, instead of the "proclamations" that were too many to count about *aliyah* from the countries of plenty, whose prospects are very slim, at least in the near future, and together with this, as experience has shown regarding the absorption of volunteers, there are not at all the conditions suitable for their absorption in the desired way. And the internal *aliyah* has dropped in the most alarming way specifically in the circles of our Sephardic brethren since their arrival in our Holy Land. And when there will be an appeal from a Sephardic woman, an appeal with enthusiasm, that they will not turn an ear at all to those who preached for small families, a preaching for many years which to our great sorrow succeeded in an exceptional way—surely such an appeal would find a correct and also deep echo and even to a change in deed. And in the same way also regarding the establishing of family life, etc., etc.
I brought an example from the matters that everyone agrees on their vitality in our Holy Land, from the edge of the left to the edge of the right. But surely the majority of our people sitting in the Holy Land has sobered up from the temptations and incitements to turn away from the path of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*, our eternal Torah. And a call to return to the source and way of life according to the Torah and its *mitzvos* "also" will find a correct echo and will bring to actions in certain circles that will go and expand and multiply, for the heart of each and every one of Israel is finally awake to our Torah and *mitzvos*, only one needs to find the point, in another style the *mitzvah*, suitable for the state of mind of a certain circle or of a certain person, and to begin regarding this circle and person with speech about this *mitzvah*, and then finally *mitzvah* drags *mitzvah*.
I know the argument and the saying, how is it possible to preach to others before the preacher himself has reached perfection in his own life. But one sees tangibly that this argument is nothing but a cover for the lack of desire for action in the aforementioned direction, for there is only One, the Almighty, and preachers have never been lacking in Israel, preachers for positive things and also for various and strange things. And furthermore and mainly, that in our period the time is too short to wait until the preacher and the motivator is perfected and then he will begin in action, and there is no advice but to do the two things at once, to preach and to motivate himself and also the environment.
My letter is long and I will summarize in short the point of the above, and it is, that it is even clearer to me than in our first meeting, and as my opinion was then so is my opinion now, that you are gifted with a talent for influence and have the possibilities for this, and it is a pity for every day that passes and you do not activate your talent in the direction to return the youth and the young people, and how good also the adults although the matter is more difficult, to positive life,

## 243

life worthy of its name, life according to our Torah and its *mitzvos* of which it is said, "And he (the Jewish people) shall live by them," and one hour earlier is better.
(From a letter, 5 Elul, 5767)

...I acknowledge receipt of your book *Avnei Derech*, with the introduction of a request for much forgiveness for the delay in the acknowledgment due to several reasons. And thank you for your attentiveness in sending your book, and the creation of a person—to a significant extent reflects the author, and especially since this book also contains details from the history of the days of his life, and in distance of place—there is in this also a matter of personal acquaintance with the author of the book.
I am accustomed to think, when receiving a book from an author, that it was not "in vain" that he sent me his book and surely the intention of the author is that I should examine his book and if I will have something to comment—he will accept my comments in the spirit of the matter even if I do not identify with the worldview of the author. And so regarding your book I will permit myself to note a few comments, and especially—in the internal point of the book, the depiction of the *kvutzah* (group) and the life of the *kvutzah*, a subject to which you dedicate your book in particular.
I hope that you will agree that the matter of the *kvutzah* is not a goal in itself, and it goes without saying the final goal; but its purpose is to achieve a desired and hoped-for order of life through collective cooperation.
In itself, the matter of the *kvutzah* is, seemingly, to equate the small and the great, which is in essence the opposite of the nature of man; for human beings, just as their faces are not similar so their opinions are not similar to one another. And therefore the individual finds satisfaction and perfection when it is possible for him to bring to action everything that he has in potential, and in the fullest measure, not so much in the common matters that he has with the members of his society, but specifically in his individual area in which he excels from his friends and his environment, for this is his selfhood. On the other hand, man is not by nature a loner and "it is not good for man to be alone," and he seeks a life of society in which and through which and with its help he can reach his own perfection.
From the aforementioned assumption, on the one hand the life of the *kvutzah* has great importance in that they form a background for the sharing of powers of several people and through this to greater achievements, and of course, even from the sum of all the private powers, and as is known that the activity of two people together is greater than double the activity of each one of them separately. And also from the positive matters in the *kvutzah* is that it removes that undesirable jealousy and competition that brings frequent deterioration of the relations between man and his fellow, whereas collective action generally brings hearts closer, etc.
On the other hand, the purpose of the *kvutzah* is not to cancel all competition in general, for one

## 244

of the matters that awaken to extra efforts and to progress and utilization of all the powers and with alacrity, etc.—is specifically from this that a person has a challenge and competition. But the *kvutzah* must channel the natural competition to a higher area. In other words, instead of that in an individualistic society the competition begins in the simplest needs, the physical and material, and until, in the language of our Sages of blessed memory, "were it not for the fear (of the kingdom (—the necessity of society)) one man would swallow his fellow alive," here in the *kvutzah* it is possible to transfer this power to greater achievements, whether in an addition much beyond the necessary needs or in a higher area—in the life of the spirit.
The conclusion from the above is that the matter of the *kvutzah* and the life of the *kvutzah* is not a goal and achievement in itself, but a stage and preparation and path for the development of the individuality and the uniqueness that is in each and every one and their realization in the best way and in the fullest measure.
This fundamental evaluation of the matter of the *kvutzah* touches not only after they have already achieved a full collective order of life and one needs to decide in practice how to utilize the advantage of the powers and how to highlight in each one his private traits and talents in their full scope, but it touches also immediately at the beginning of the life of the *kvutzah*, since often and perhaps also in most times, the very order of the life of the *kvutzah* must, as mentioned, awaken internal resistance against the order and the regime that tries to subdue the individual as an individual and to turn him into a part of the block, i.e., the *kvutzah*. In contrast, if the individual knows that this is nothing but a stage in his development and the path that increases his possibility to reach greater individual achievements, by this that they free him from worries at a lower stage than this (regarding his necessary needs that are achieved more easily and without wasting powers and time thanks to the collective joint action), then this recognition will not only cancel his natural resistance but will even add to him enthusiasm and dedication in the fulfillment of his tasks in the *kvutzah*.
The above touches not only on the success of the *kvutzah* in general, but also on the content of life and the way of life in the *kvutzah*, which you also touch on in your book, such as the relations between parents and children and the like (and more so—that the damage is liable to be greater than the reward in this area), since these relations are in the area of the "spiritual" life of man in which the independence of the individual is important and essential.
There is another point, which in my opinion is important, and it is in the change of feeling and attitude toward the *kvutzah* on the part of the founders of the *kvutzah* and on the part of those who were born in the *kvutzah*. For if the founders of the *kvutzah*, or those who came to the life of the *kvutzah* from close by relatively, can receive mental satisfaction in recognizing that they reached this, as you write, from a life absolutely and completely different, and from an environment permeated with an opposite worldview, and they achieved a life of *kvutzah* out of toil and labor and sacrifices and hardships, etc., that all this adds value and admiration to the achieved thing, here those who were born in the *kvutzah* or were raised in it see this order of life as natural, and for these surely the limitations of the life of the *kvutzah*, which were mentioned above, are more prominent than the positive sides, which is bound to awaken in them mental dissatisfaction or even rebellion, and in any case frictions, toward those who force upon them a collective regime (and the highlighting of the *kvutzah* as a stage and preparation—also in this it will help).

## 245

And from here the piercing problem, which by the way I did not find in your book an answer to: what do they "give" to the generation born in the *kvutzah* as a goal or ideal that they will want to reach even out of toil and labor and self-sacrifice within the framework of the life of society?
And last but not least, it is understood that I read with interest at the end of your book the "Chapters of Life." And also in this I will permit myself to come with a comment, that it is a pity and a shame that you did not include in these autobiographical notes—a note about the "source" as a result of which you wore a *kippah* at the time you read verses of *Tanach* in the Knesset, especially—that surely you guessed in advance that there would be a reaction from the left, a negative reaction, and in spite of this you did a great deed, and the foundation for this is surely rooted and placed in the beginning of the days of your life, in the house of father or grandfather, and the like.
As is the way of the children of Israel to integrate and connect the matters that they discuss with the days of the year, and especially days of *moed* and *chag*, here also on Rosh Hashanah our Sages of blessed memory emphasized man as an individual, and not only on the first Rosh Hashanah, the day G-d created the first man, but as a teaching and emphasis of our Sages: "Therefore man was created alone, to teach you (that in all generations and in all places) one soul is like an entire world," and they continued further in this an explanation that not one of them is similar to his fellow, therefore each and every one is obligated to say, "For my sake the world was created." In other words, specifically in this that no man is similar to his fellow is he important as an entire world (*Sanhedrin*, end of chapter 4). This matter served also as a central point for my letter for Rosh Hashanah attached here, which I hope will interest you.
(From a letter, days of *Selichos*, 5724)

Your letter, in which you propose to me to write an article about the new English translation of the Torah, has reached me with a significant delay. I am sorry that also from my side my answer was inevitably delayed.
I thank you for the invitation, but as is known, it is generally not my way to write articles for the press, and I cannot make any exception in this. If there appears from me an address in the press from time to time, it carries a general character and is in no case exclusively for any press organ. You will therefore excuse me that I cannot accept your friendly invitation.
As far as my personal attitude toward this translation is concerned, it is self-evident that the declaration of the *Agudas HaRabbanim*, which relies naturally on the *halachah*, is decisive and leaves no room for doubts in the matter.
With respect and a wish
for a happy Purim,
P.S.


## נשא

## 263

### Naso

In response to your letter from the 19th of Teves, which was received after a long delay, in which you write several questions regarding the laws and customs of Israel.

In general, it is not my practice to issue halachic rulings, nor is there any need for this, as there are many *morei hora’ah* in your city to whom you can turn; they will explain the questions in all their details (which are often difficult to commit to writing in a letter).

Nevertheless, since you have already written, I will at least answer the first question, in the way you phrased it, regarding the matter of a woman covering her hair, and upon what the custom relies, etc.

Know that this is a definitive law in our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and not merely a custom (though even a custom of Israel carries great importance). Furthermore, even among the laws, there is a special importance to the fulfillment of this law—the covering of a woman’s hair (a married woman, of course)—as is understood from the magnitude of the reward for fulfilling this law. In its precise language [copied in the commentaries on *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chaim*, section 75 (where this law of hair covering is explained in detail)—the punishment is also mentioned there, but I choose to copy that which concerns the reward], the passage from the holy *Zohar* of *Parshas Naso* (copied in the *Mishnah Berurah*, *Hilchos Krias Shema*, section 75) states: "Her children will be elevated and distinguished above all other people of the world, and not only that, but her husband will be blessed with all the blessings from above and blessings from below, in wealth, in children, and in children’s children, etc."

To add to what has been said: it is a great wonder regarding anyone who has a spark of faith in their heart and desires that their life after marriage be truly happy—regarding the husband, the wife, and their children, whom Hashem will bless.

Is there really any room for this discomfort (even if we were to say that there is discomfort) that comes with covering the hair, in comparison to the blessing from Hashem, the Creator of man, the Creator of the world, and its Guide?! This is a light-headedness like no other, even if there were a doubt or a double doubt regarding the necessity of the matter, and all the more so regarding a matter that is explicit.

It is understood that I am aware of the objection to the above, for there are many who do not observe this law. However, this objection has existed for thousands of years: "You are the fewest of all the peoples," and how is it that their laws are different from every other nation? To our great sorrow, even within *Bnei Yisrael* one can find those who, for the time being, desecrate the Shabbos in public, and even to the point of intermarriage, *r"l*. It is simple that this does not detract, *chas v'shalom*, in the slightest from the vitality of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and its *mitzvos*, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them." Just as the making of the Golden Calf in its time (and in close proximity to the time of the Giving of the Torah) did not detract in the slightest from the vitality of the Ten Commandments, and subsequently the entire Torah and its *mitzvos*, down to our own generation.

And as we find ourselves a few days before the days of Purim, this—as mentioned above—was the argument of

## 264

Haman, and his conclusion was not only the loss of the spiritual life of the people of Israel, but to destroy all the Jews, from young to old, children and women.

For the existence of *Bnei Yisrael* in every place they are is solely through the Torah and its *mitzvos*, which were given by the One Hashem to the one nation in the land.

(From a letter dated 24 Adar, 5725)

. . . And regarding your asking for my opinion on the matter of hair covering, I am astonished by the question, especially in the form you write—that she will wear a *paruk* (wig) such that the entire head will be covered, with only two fingers' width in the front exposed. It is not understood whom one is trying to deceive with this, for it is obvious that it is not the Almighty, and not even the world, but rather oneself. And what benefit is there in such a thing?

It is understood that this is only as a last resort, for the law is explicit in the *Shulchan Aruch*, and consequently, there is no room for question or doubt. I am confident that through pleasant ways, speaking about it time and again, the person in question will agree to the desired view on this. . .

(From a letter dated 28 Elul, 5714)

. . . Regarding what you wrote about covering your hair—there is no question here at all. Since Hashem said clearly that it is for the good of the woman, her husband, and their children, *sheyichyu*, that her head hair should not be exposed—it is certainly so. It is impossible that through the fulfillment of a *mitzvah* of Hashem, a headache or the like would come about!

Regarding your writing that when you wear a *sheitel* (wig) the aforementioned pain occurs, it is possible: 1) That this is a lie of the *Yetzer Hara*, which does not want you to fulfill *mitzvos* and does not want blessings to come to Jews. 2) If it is true—this is proof that it is for your own good to cut your hair so that it will be short, and then there will certainly be no pain from the *sheitel*.

It is a wonder that after you have seen the blessing of Hashem and His miracles in the birth of your son, *sheyichye*, you are asking about this matter!

In my secretariat, they do not write in French, therefore the response comes in *Lashon HaKodesh*, but you may write in French in the future, as I read this language.

(From a letter dated 22 Teves, 5744)

## 266

In many details, even though they saw tangibly the great destruction caused by the lack of attention given to women and girls, in addition to what our Sages (*Shemos Rabbah*) said: that Hashem said at the Giving of the Torah, "Thus shall you say to the house of Yaakov" (the women) first, and afterwards "you shall speak to the children of Israel." The proof of this is that in the *mitzvah* of the Tree of Knowledge, it was not so, and it caused what it caused until the end of all generations.

It is understood that my intention here is not to preach, but that he should seek advice and letters that will clarify the situation as it is, even in these matters to which they have not been accustomed until now. . .

(From a letter dated 6 Teves, 5715)

I read with astonishment in your letter that it is as if, *chas v'shalom*, there is a *kapida* (resentment) against you, etc.

It is understood that there is no basis for this. As I have written to others, in general, I see no benefit in *kapida*. It may be that at times there is sorrow from undesirable conduct, or from the fact that one does not utilize the blessing and success that Hashem gives, and it pains the heart that matters could be better than they are, and because of trivial things, one does not utilize the blessings of Hashem.

From this, it is understood that *kapida* is the exact opposite, and all the more so. However, the sorrow mentioned above does have a place in your matter. But that has no connection to reading into my letter that which was not written, or that because of this the answer is being withheld (which is mostly due to being very busy).

And I mean by this what I think I have already written to you: the matter of the *sheitel* in your home. As I have, I believe, hinted to you, the matter does not change, and it is certainly not rectified, by one turning a blind eye to it; and before Hashem, all hidden things are revealed. And the sorrow in connection with this is understandable, according to the holy *Zohar* (brought in the *Acharonim*, *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*), Part 3, 126a: "A woman should cover herself with the modesty of the house" (from this it is understood how much more so outside the house), "and if she does so... her children will be elevated and distinguished... and she will be blessed with everything, with blessings from above and blessings from below, in wealth, in children, and in children’s children." See there well.

I want to emphasize once again that there is not a shred of a *kapida* here, but rather frustration and pain, which is only increased when one thinks about the *mesiras nefesh*, so to speak, that the desired conduct requires in relation to the loss, and even more so when taking into account the place where

## 267

one finds oneself now, where such good conduct can influence many Jewish families to begin to follow suit and go "from strength to strength."

May it be the will that, in the end, each of us should see how the Holy One, Blessed be He, bestows blessing and success in both material and spiritual matters, and that we should make all the necessary *keilim* (vessels) to receive and utilize the blessing to the fullest extent.

And coming from the month of redemption, the month of Tammuz, the redemption of our Rebbe, our Nasi—and "the body follows the head"—may each of us be redeemed, immediately and completely, from all confusing matters, and be able to serve Hashem with joy and a good heart.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

(From a letter dated 5 Menachem Av, 5718)

I received your letter in which you write about what was conveyed to you in my name, and you answer that there are details you agree with and details you do not want, and consequently, it would be a matter of coercion, etc.

This entire approach is not correct or appropriate when approaching the beginning of a life order. It is clear that everyone wants their life to be happy, and happiness in life depends in quality and quantity specifically on the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. The question is not what a person wants or does not want, but rather the approach is: on what does a person's happiness depend, upon whom does it depend, and under what conditions can one hope that happiness will actually come?

I said to [name] when he was here that a man's wife can be a help to him or against him. Even though it is difficult to estimate in advance and know with one hundred percent certainty how the relationship will be over decades, a known and important criterion in this is the relationship between the young couple and the consideration of their outlooks—of one person toward the other before the wedding. He must clarify this (as must everyone who wishes to enter into the covenant of marriage) as much as possible.

Regarding him, he should not hide anything from her regarding his current outlook on life, and he should ask her to tell him clearly what her attitude is toward his outlook. If she acts as she wrote in her letter—that she will arrange her life according to her own desires without considering the opinion of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and the instructions He gave to every man and woman of the people of Israel—one must reflect very carefully on the question of the marriage and the *shidduch* in general.

Since [name] wanted to know my opinion on this, and also my agreement—and as I also expressed my blessing—I, for my part, can agree with a whole heart when I see the maximum possible hope that their lives will be happy. This depends on them arranging their lives on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvah* as they

## 268

are stated in the *Shulchan Aruch*, and not according to the interpretation of each individual, where for this detail one agrees and for other details one does not agree. For the Holy One, Blessed be He, says that walking in His ways, which He has taught, guarantees life with blessing and success, whereas walking in other ways does not. I cannot take upon myself the responsibility of participating in such a matter when one of the parties approaches the whole thing saying they do not want it, do not promise it, and are being coerced against their will, etc.

If someone says that they cannot concede and walk specifically with hair covering, with a headscarf or a *sheitel*, and it makes no difference to them if by doing so they endanger their happiness and the happiness of the other party in their shared life for decades, then such a person has no sense of responsibility, nor appropriate appreciation or knowledge of what a shared life is, and how much it is worth conceding even on more important matters, provided that the life be united and happy. As mentioned, this is impossible in the life of a Jewish man and woman except through Torah and *mitzvah*.

May the Holy One, Blessed be He, grant her the merit to recognize her path in life and to decide for her own good—the true good, which is good both materially and spiritually—and that, in truth, one is impossible without the other.

(From a letter dated 10 Sivan, 5714)


## בהעלותך

## 270

...And with a blessing for the fulfillment of what is written: "For the lips of a Kohen shall guard knowledge..." 
It may be said that this refers to the service of the Leviim to the Kohanim, which is done in silence — the *shirah* (an acronym for *shirut* [service] and *shirah* [song]) of the lips.
(From a letter, Yemei Elul 5750)

I was pleased to learn from the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal affairs, a *mashpia*, and a director, Rabbi R. regarding the order of their study and *avodah*, and the beginning of what they are doing in this regard with the help of Hashem.

However, on the other hand, it caused me pain and distress that it appears that due to the thoughts regarding the question of the transcription, there is a lack of sufficient *tzugitragkeit* (dedication/application) and the depth necessary and required for the study of Torah in general, and for the study of the teachings of Chassidus and engagement in the *avodah* of *tefillah* in particular.

And although time does not permit me to go into this at length, nevertheless, due to the importance of the matter, I am writing the following few lines:

Surely you are familiar with the *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who explained the process of the journeys of the Bnei Yisrael in the desert: that from journey to journey, they would dismantle the *Mishkan* and then set it up in a new place. It is stated in the verse that the time they spent in each encampment was not uniform. As the verse states: "And there were times when the cloud remained from evening until morning, and the cloud rose in the morning and they journeyed; or by day and by night... or two days, or a month, or a year." Yet, in all the journeys, the common denominator was that it was "by the word of Hashem, by the hand of Moshe." That is to say, there was no change or difference in the setting up of the *Mishkan* and in all matters of the service of Hashem, whether they stayed in a place for a year or several years, or whether they stayed in a place for only a day and a night, or even just from evening until morning.

This is also understood by human intellect, and even by the intellect of the *nefesh habehamis*: since they encamp according to the word of Hashem and journey according to the word of Hashem — which is above time and above space — and yet the purpose of creation in general, and the journeys in particular, is to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in physical time and space, then we have nothing to do but fulfill the will of our Creator and thereby connect and cleave to the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He. He will do as He wills, whether it be to remain in this place for many years or only from evening until morning. And since one’s involvement in this is in that which is above time and above space, the difference in the duration of time does not affect him at all.

Based on this, one can also explain what is stated in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 26, that this unification above is eternal forever and ever, etc., and likewise the revelation of His will in His speech, which is the Torah, is eternal. And there is also an additional explanation here for what is brought in many places in the revealed Torah regarding matters that require a *shiur* (measure): that if it is a matter of a *mitzvah*, the *mitzvah* itself renders it significant, as if it possessed a physical measure.

My hope is strong that these few words of mine will suffice, and I will be happy to receive good news soon that you are increasing in Torah and *avodah*, both in yourselves and in your influence upon others. And surely the promise of our Sages, of blessed memory, will be fulfilled in them:

## 271

"A person who sanctifies himself a little from below, they sanctify him (a promise) much from above."
With a blessing for success in Torah study and in *yiras shamayim*.
(From a letter, 11 Iyar, 5713)


## שלח

## 271

### Shelach

I acknowledge receipt of the information regarding your upcoming annual luncheon on Sunday, Parshas Shelach, may it be successful in every respect.

It is a well-known teaching of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, that the weekly Parsha contains guidance for daily life, especially in connection with extraordinary events.

This year’s event takes place during the week of Parshas Shelach, which recounts how Moshe Rabbeinu sent scouts to survey Eretz Yisrael, and how those scouts brought back a negative report. Our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us that the women were not deterred by this unfavorable report; they continued to desire to reach Eretz Yisrael, Eretz HaKodesh, in accordance with the will of the Ribono shel Olam. The women were imbued with the feeling that Eretz Yisrael is a land of holiness and special Divine providence, as the Torah states: "A land which Hashem your G-d cares for; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

As has been emphasized many times, the Torah is eternal, and all its instructions are eternal—meaning they are valid everywhere and at all times.

## 272

The attachment of the Jewish woman to "Eretz HaKodesh" is an expression of her dedication to all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, which manifests in an even stronger form than that of men, from time to time.

From this, there is also guidance for our generation: that women can accomplish much to strengthen all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos—first and foremost in their own homes, and together with that, in their surroundings in an appropriate manner—and in this way, create within their homes and their surroundings an "Eretz HaKodesh" for the Divine Shechinah.

This is, after all, one of the tasks of Chabad women everywhere, who possess the additional special merit that their path is illuminated by the light of Chassidus and Chassidic traditions.

And just as, together with Eretz Yisrael, all the Divine blessings of a "land flowing with milk and honey" were given—also in the material sense—provided that one conducts oneself according to the will of the Ribono shel Olam, so too are all Divine blessings always prepared for everyone who helps to strengthen and spread Torah-Yiddishkeit to the fullest extent of their capabilities.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to your work in an ever-increasing measure, and may He bless you with revealed and manifest good in everything you need, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With blessings for good tidings.
(From a letter dated 13 Sivan, 5725)

...Regarding what you wrote, that there are those who mock him—it is nothing new that people mock those who observe Torah and mitzvos. This was the lot of many who were zealous for the word of Hashem, beginning with Avraham Avinu. See the beginning (and foundation) of all of Shulchan Aruch: "And he should not be ashamed..." And it has already been said: "Hashem is with us; do not fear them."
(From a letter dated 23 MarCheshvan, 5723)


## כח סיון

## 275

These institutions [were established] during the final ten years of the Rebbe’s life in this world, and they continue to grow in light even after his passing, in a manner of "ascending in holiness".
