The core explanation for this—based on the well-known principle that "a descent is for the sake of an ascent"—is as follows: Since the move to the lower hemisphere, the "American exile", constituted an extremely great descent [in addition to the descent of the other exiles, where "Lubavitch went into exile"], it is understood that the intent and purpose behind it is the subsequent ascent, reaching an incomparable ascent (corresponding to the incomparable descent). This is the addition and innovation achieved in the general work of "let your springs spread outward" specifically in the lower hemisphere, in a more elevated manner, reaching even to the level of the incomparable.

Yet, there still remains a need to explain the connection of this matter to the content of the work of "let your springs spread outward"—the "slogan" of the teachings of Chassidus in general, and Chabad Chassidus in particular. Since every matter is by Divine Providence, and Hashem orchestrated the circumstances so that the center of Chabad Chassidus—the Rebbe and his Chassidim—was transferred and planted in the lower hemisphere, it must be said that this relates specifically to the perfection of the matter of "let your springs spread outward."

b. This can be understood by first explaining the precision of the language (and content) of "let your springs spread outward" (*yifu tzu mayanosecha chutzah*):

Since this phrasing is a verse in the Written Torah, where every single word is of the utmost precision, it is understood that in the work of "let your springs spread outward" there is a special emphasis (and instruction) in each of these three words (in addition to the general content contained in all of them together).

Furthermore: Every expression in the "Torah of Truth" is directed toward the true content of the expression, as it exists in the utmost perfection, and even in an unlimited manner. From this, it is also understood regarding our subject, that the intent in each of these three words—"spread" (*yifu tzu*), "your springs" (*mayanosecha*), and "outward" (*chutzah*)—is to the full meaning of the word, even in an unlimited manner.

It can be said that the same applies to the addition in "let your springs spread outward" that comes about through (the redemption of 12 Tammuz and through) the transfer to the lower hemisphere: (a) an addition in every detail of these three matters; (b) and the addition in each one of them is a true addition in an unlimited manner (as will be explained in section 7).

c. Explanation of the matter:

## 277

To the matters as they are in their root and source, the essence of Torah—the "hidden of the Torah" (the inner dimension of the Torah) which connects with the "hidden of Hashem", reaching up to His very Essence and Being.

In addition to this, it can be said that "your springs" refers to the person who is spreading—that his engagement in the work of "let your springs spread outward" must be not only with his revealed faculties (as they have already been drawn down from their root and source), for then his engagement in this is with measurement and limitation, but also with his hidden faculties as they are included in their root and source in the essence of the soul ("your springs"), for then his engagement in this is in a manner that is above measurement and limitation.

e. "Outward" (*chutzah*):

In the general reality of the world, there are two parts: "inside" (*panim*) and "outside" (*chutz*). And in each of them there are many levels: from the innermost of the inside to the outermost of the outside, until the "outward" beyond which there is no further outward. From this, it is also understood regarding the "outward" in our case, that it has several levels: relative to the level of "your springs," even matters of holiness (even high levels of holiness, but lower than the level of "your springs") are called "outward"; and there is "outward" in its literal sense—matters that are outside the boundary of holiness, and within them themselves there are also many levels, until the "outward" beyond which there is no further outward.

And "outward" in the language of the Torah (the Torah of Truth) means—"outward" without any limitations, which includes also the "outward" beyond which there is no further outward (similar to "down, down, until there is no end"); meaning, that the work of "let your springs spread" must be in all the levels of "outward," even in the "outward" beyond which there is no further outward.

f. It can be said that these three matters are dependent upon one another:

When a person's engagement in studying and spreading the teachings of Chassidus is from the "essence" of his soul, which is above measurement and limitation, then the Torah that he teaches and spreads is also without limitations, until there remains no matter for him (even the most elevated matters in the Torah, up to the "essence" of the Torah) that does not spread outward; and the revelation of the essence of the soul (and through this—the essence of the Torah) is brought about by the "outward"—as explained in the continuation of the *hillula*, that in order to win the war ("for the victory is planted and rooted in the essence of the soul, higher than the revealed faculties in the soul"), "(the King) spends all the treasures of the precious wealth collected and gathered over many years from generation to generation, and which from time immemorial

## 279

In its truth and perfection, meaning, everything that is included in "send" (*shelach*). For, if there is a specific detail that is included in the meaning of "send," and it has not yet been done in practice—this is not "send" in its truth and perfection.

It can be said that (in general) there are three matters in this—corresponding to the three matters of "spread," "your springs," and "outward":

(a) The manner of the action of the mission—in spreading without any limitations, for as long as the action of the mission can be in greater spreading, it cannot be said that the manner of the action in this is in its truth; and in the terminology mentioned above—the truth of the matter of "spread."

(b) The thing (the person who sends, and the Torah) that is sent from him—not just an external or intermediate thing, etc., but the most elevated thing, up to the root and source and essence of the thing, for as long as there is a more elevated level (in it itself, and in the Torah) that he has not sent, it is still not "send" in its truth; and in the terminology mentioned above—the truth of the matter of "your springs."

(c) The place to which one sends—not only in proximity of place, but also in distance of place, and not only distance of place relative to him, but the most distant place than which there is none more distant, for as long as there is a more distant place, then the mission "outward" has not yet been done in its truth; and in the terminology mentioned above—the truth of the matter of "outward."

ix. And according to the words of the Rebbe in his letter for the first celebration of 12 Tammuz —"Hashem did not redeem only me on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, the observers of mitzvos, and also those who are called by the name of Israel," it is understood that everything stated above regarding the elevation achieved in the work of "let your springs spread outward" through the transfer to the lower hemisphere—which came as a result of the redemption of 12-13 Tammuz—belongs to every single Jew, even to the one "who is called by the name of Israel".

And simply—that for each and every one there must be the matter and the work of "send," "let your springs spread outward"—through the power of the Nasi of the generation, who placed a mission ("send") upon each and every one to engage in spreading the springs outward.

And more specifically—in all three matters mentioned: "spread"—that the study reaches and penetrates into all parts of the place where one teaches this Torah. And also regarding the Torah that one spreads—one should not think,


## קרח

## 281

### Korach

... *Tashar, tashar* [a term of praise/encouragement] for your great efforts regarding the technical religious front, and for the fact that you did not refrain even from going to [the authorities/the relevant office], etc. And surely, in a case such as this, even for a doubt or a double doubt, one should act, as evidenced by *Sanhedrin* (110a), and especially according to the opinion of the Ramban (in his commentary on the Eighth Principle of the Rambam’s *Sefer HaMitzvos*), according to which [the verse] "And Moshe arose and went," etc....

## חוקת

## 281

### Chukas

Following up on our previous conversations regarding your efforts to secure the necessary funds for printing the Tanya.

You will surely inform us of the results of your efforts in this matter. It is unnecessary to elaborate on the great necessity of this project and its lofty value, and I have a strong hope that you will do everything in your power regarding this, for "merit is brought about through those who are meritorious"—

The refinement of the atmosphere of the world through the letters of Torah and tefillah, the *tola* and *tola'as* of the *parah* (red heifer) ritual, as explained in *Likutei Torah* in the *maamar* beginning "Zos Chukas" (section 4).

And it may be said that in the study of Tanya—which is a collection of advice for the *avodah* of the heart—there are two aspects:

Through one who is *zakai* (meritorious)—and it is worth noting the distinction between Kohanim and Levi'im, where the Levi'im are the level of *tahor* (pure).

(From a letter, Erev Shabbos Parshas Parah, 5705)


## פינחס

## 296

### Pinchas

Regarding the point raised from *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Pinchas*, *dih* "Kodesh Yisrael," page 284, where the text appears several times as "Kodesh HaAdam" (the person is holy), and you expressed surprise, as it should surely be "Yisrael" (Israel is holy):

You must be using an old edition; this has already been corrected in subsequent printings. It appears that due to fear of the censor, it was initially printed as "HaAdam."

See *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Shemos*, page 86, and the notes there.

May the Ribono shel Olam turn these days into gladness and joy, and may it be revealed to the eyes of all flesh that "Israel is holy to Hashem... all who devour him shall be held guilty," speedily in our days.

(From a letter dated 6 Menachem Av, the Ribono shel Olam)

### Bein HaMetzarim

And establish the *chazakah* — regarding the matter and the *shakla v'tarya* there in the *halachos* of *Zeman HaMizman* and the *halachos* of *Beis HaBechirah* (and *Ohr Torah*, *Parshas Pinchas*).

And this is the essential *din* and *minhag* during *Bein HaMetzarim*: not only to nullify them, but to transform them into gladness and joy and *moadim tovim* ("And they loved truth and peace" — as is also written in his introduction to his sefer, which was printed in *Torah Temimah*, attached here is 10 dollars).

And fortunate is the portion of each and every publisher of *dinim* and *minhagim* that are relevant for practical application. And in the conclusion of his introduction — specifically for the time to come, three cities of refuge will be added. And the *kav* of the Arizal is known regarding this — a *tikkun* for the first brothers, Kayin and Hevel, and reaching perfection — through love and unity.

I will mention this at the *tziyon*.
(From a letter, 23 Tammuz, 5747)

Cutting hair — it should be postponed until after *Bein HaMetzarim*. Regarding what is practiced to be stringent, etc. — from the day the three years are completed...
(From a letter, 4 Tammuz, 5727)

## 298

... Regarding the second question: a) You apparently think that our Sages did not properly appreciate the greatness of Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai. This is not so. It suffices to cite two or three places:
1) Regarding his knowledge of Torah and the sciences: (*Maseches Sofrim*, ch. 16) If all the heavens were parchment, all the trees were quills, and all the seas were ink, it would not be sufficient to record the wisdom he learned from his teachers. 2) Regarding worldly matters and the conduct of the state: (end of *Sotah*) When Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai died, the luster of wisdom ceased (referring to worldly wisdom, *Maharsha*). 3) As a leader of Israel: (*Sifri*, end of *Parshas Berachah*) Moshe was in Egypt for 40 years, in Midian for 40 years, and sustained Israel for 40 years. Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai engaged in business for 40 years, served the Sages for 40 years, and sustained Israel (he was *Nasi*) for 40 years.

b) Regarding the assessment of the events during the time of the *Churban*, the political situation then, the mood of the Romans, whether there was hope for peace, etc. — how is it possible for us, who are removed from that time by more than 1,800 years and have almost no reliable documentation other than the Talmud from that era, to offer an opinion that does not agree, even in a minor detail, with the opinion of people who lived in that generation or the one that followed? This would be true even if it were written in a simple history book. Now that this assessment has entered the Talmud — meaning that through *Hashgachah* from above it became part of the *Torah Shebe'al Peh*, whose holiness is the holiness of *Torah Shebe'al Peh* — there is no room for *shakla v'tarya* as to whether it is true; rather, the only task is to strive to understand the matter and explain it, so that we, too, may understand it.

c) A decisive proof that Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai did not view the decree of the *Churban* as something that could not be averted, but rather that he was striving even then to save the *Beis HaMikdash* from destruction, is the fact that before he went to Vespasian, he strove [with] the leaders of Jerusalem at that time to make peace with the Romans. And only when he did not succeed in this did he go to Vespasian, to strive with the words of Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai, "perhaps there will be a small salvation"...
(From a letter, end of Elul, 5708)

## אופנים

## Ofanim and Seraphim, their distinction.

The distinction between Ofanim and Seraphim is as follows:

The Ofanim are associated with the attribute of *Malchus*, as it is written, "And I looked, and behold, four wheels (*Ofanim*) beside the *Keruvim*." This reflects the aspect of *bittul* that comes from the realization of *Malchus*—the recognition that "there is nothing else besides Him," which is the level of *bittul* that characterizes the *Olam HaAsiyah*.

The Seraphim, by contrast, are associated with the attribute of *Gevurah* and *Eish* (fire), as it is written, "Seraphim stood above Him." Their *avodah* is one of *ratzo*—a burning, intense yearning to be consumed within the light of the *Ein Sof*.

Thus, the difference between them is the difference between the *bittul* of *Malchus*—which is a state of standing in place and acknowledging the sovereignty of Hashem—and the *bittul* of *Gevurah*, which is a state of active, fiery movement toward the Source.

## אייר

## Iyar and Nissan — Doing Good and Turning Away from Evil

The month of Iyar follows the month of Nissan. In the order of the avodah of the soul, this corresponds to the sequence of "turn away from evil and do good" (Tehillim 34:15).

Nissan is the time of "turn away from evil"—the process of *iskafya* (subjugation) and *is'hapcha* (transformation) of the *sitra achra*. This is the essence of the exodus from Mitzrayim, which is the "turning away" from the constraints and limitations of the *kelipah*.

Iyar, however, is the time of "do good." It is the period of *sefirat ha'omer*, which is a process of refinement and purification of the seven *middos*—the "doing" of good through the rectification of one's character traits and the elevation of the *nefesh habahamit*.

Thus, the transition from Nissan to Iyar represents the movement from the initial liberation—the departure from the negative—to the constructive building of one's *avodah*, where the *neshamah* actively engages in the refinement of the world, transforming the "good" that is hidden within the material into a dwelling place for Hashem.

## ברכת הגומל

## Birchas HaGomel

 The Gemara states that one who has been saved from four situations must recite Birchas HaGomel: those who have traveled across the sea, those who have traveled through the desert, one who has recovered from an illness, and one who has been released from prison. 

Seemingly, we must understand the common denominator between these four. While it is true that all four involve a state of danger from which one has been rescued, the nature of the danger differs significantly. Furthermore, the Gemara derives these four from the verse in Tehillim, "He sent His word and healed them, and delivered them from their destructions," which implies that the common thread is the concept of "healing" and "deliverance."

But in truth, the matter can be understood by looking at the deeper significance of these four categories within the context of *avodah*. The four categories represent the four primary obstacles that a person encounters in their *avodah* to Hashem:

The "sea" represents the turbulence of the world—the *he'elem v'hester* (concealment) that threatens to overwhelm the *neshamah* as it descends into the body. The "desert" represents the desolate places where there is no *yishuv* (settlement) of *kedushah*, where one is left to navigate without the support of a *kehillah* or the light of Torah. "Illness" refers to the weakening of the *kochos* of the soul, where the *yetzer hara* gains strength through the person’s own spiritual lethargy. And "prison" refers to the state of being constrained by the *gashmius* of the world, where the *neshamah* is unable to express its innate *bitul* and *dveikus* to Hashem.

When a person overcomes these challenges—whether through their own *avodah* or through the *chesed* of Hashem—they are essentially experiencing a "redemption" from the limitations of their own nature. Birchas HaGomel is the acknowledgment that this rescue is not merely a physical survival, but a spiritual rebirth. It is the declaration that the *Ribono shel Olam* has bestowed "good" upon one who is undeserving, recognizing that even when one is trapped in the "sea" or the "desert" of their own making, the *Ohr Ein Sof* remains accessible, waiting to deliver them from their "destructions."

## כסלו, י&quot;ט כסלו

## Kislev, 19 Kislev

 The concept of 19 Kislev—the "Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus"—is fundamentally connected to the revelation of the inner dimension of Torah, which is the "soul of Torah." As is known, the revelation of the inner dimension of Torah is the preparation for the coming of Moshiach, as it is written, "When your springs spread outward" (*Mishlei 5:16*).

The connection between the revelation of Chassidus and the redemption is not merely a chronological sequence, but an essential one. The *avodah* of the Alter Rebbe, which culminated in his liberation on 19 Kislev, brought about a new light in the world—a light that enables every Yid, regardless of their level, to connect to the deepest levels of Elokus. This is the essence of the "spreading of the springs": that the deepest, most concealed aspects of the Torah and of Hashem’s essence are brought down into the practical reality of our daily lives, transforming the world into a dwelling place for Him.

Therefore, the celebration of 19 Kislev is not merely a commemoration of a historical event, but an ongoing *avodah*. It is a call to action for every Chossid to internalize the teachings of Chassidus and to live with the consciousness that we are standing on the threshold of the true and complete Geulah. Through our *avodah* of *bitul* and *dveikus*, and through the dissemination of these teachings to others, we hasten the day when the knowledge of Hashem will cover the earth as the waters cover the sea.

## סיון

## Regarding the custom not to say Tachanun until the 12th of Sivan

In the Shulchan Aruch it is ruled that Tachanun is not recited from Rosh Chodesh Sivan until the 12th of Sivan. The reason for this is that these days are associated with the days of the dedication of the Mizbeiach by the Nesi'im, as the 12th of Sivan is the day that concludes the period during which one can bring the Korban Pesach Sheini and the days of the dedication of the Mizbeiach.

Seemingly, however, we must understand: Why is the custom to refrain from saying Tachanun specifically until the 12th of Sivan? If the reason is the dedication of the Mizbeiach, which lasted for twelve days, then the days of the dedication were the first twelve days of Nissan. Why, then, is this custom observed in Sivan?

Furthermore, even if we say that the days of Sivan are connected to the dedication of the Mizbeiach, the dedication itself took place in Nissan. What is the connection to Sivan?

And with this we can understand:

The dedication of the Mizbeiach by the Nesi'im represents the concept of the "dedication" of the world—that the material world (the Mizbeiach, which is made of earth) becomes a dwelling place for the Shechinah. This is the ultimate purpose of the giving of the Torah, which occurred in Sivan: "The lower worlds were elevated to the higher worlds".

The twelve days of the dedication of the Mizbeiach correspond to the twelve tribes of Yisrael. Through the service of the twelve tribes, the entire world is elevated and sanctified. This service is completed and perfected through the giving of the Torah, which unites all the tribes into one entity. Therefore, the days of Sivan—the days of the giving of the Torah—are the time when the "dedication" of the world is fully realized.

Thus, the days from Rosh Chodesh Sivan until the 12th of Sivan are days of "dedication." Just as the days of the dedication of the Mizbeiach were days of joy and feasting, so too are these days in Sivan, and therefore we do not recite Tachanun.


## ר&quot;ח סיון

## Rosh Chodesh Sivan

..
See also Shavuos, the Festival of Weeks.


## י&quot;ב סיון

## 12 Sivan

 It is known that the festival of Shavuos is followed by the days of *tashlumin* (make-up days) until the 12th of Sivan. This is because the *korban chagigah* (festival offering) could be brought during these days, as the holiness of the Yom Tov extends throughout this period.

In the context of *avodah*, this teaches us that even after the actual days of Yom Tov have passed, the *hisorerus* (awakening) and the *hispaalus* (emotional arousal) experienced during the Yom Tov—specifically the *matan Torah* (giving of the Torah) that occurred on Shavuos—must continue to permeate one’s *avodah* throughout the following days.

This is the deeper meaning of the 12th of Sivan: it is the final day of the *tashlumin* period, representing the conclusion of the "extension" of the Yom Tov. The lesson is that the *bitul* and the *dveikus* to Hashem that were achieved through the *matan Torah* on Shavuos must be integrated into one’s daily life, even when one is no longer in the immediate atmosphere of the Yom Tov. This is the essence of *avodah*—to take the *taanug* and the *kedushah* of the *neshamah* and bring them down into the reality of the world, ensuring that the *hisrashmus* (impression) of Shavuos remains a constant force in one’s *avodah* of *tefillah* and *limud haTorah* throughout the entire year.


## כ&quot;ה סיון

## 28 Sivan

 The concept of the *geulah* is that it is not merely a change in the state of the world, but rather the revelation of the true reality of the world as it exists in its source. As the *Gemara* states, "The world will exist for six thousand years," and the *geulah* is the time when the purpose of this existence is realized.

On the face of it, one might ask: if the *geulah* is the ultimate purpose, why must it be preceded by the long and arduous process of *galus*? Why could the world not have been created in a state of *geulah* from the outset?

But in truth, this is the very essence of our *avodah*. Through the *avodah* of *birur*—refining the sparks of *Elokus* hidden within the material world—we transform the *galus* itself into a vessel for the *geulah*. It is not that the *geulah* arrives to replace the world; rather, the *geulah* is the result of the world itself being elevated to its state of perfection.

This is the meaning of the *maamar* of the *Chazal* regarding the *geulah*: "Everything is ready." The *avodah* of *anash* throughout the generations has already completed the refinement of the world. Therefore, the *geulah* is not a future event that we are waiting for in a passive sense; it is a reality that is already present, awaiting only the final *hisorerus* to be revealed in a manifest way.

And with this we can understand the emphasis on *mesiras nefesh* in our current time. Because we are standing at the very threshold of the *geulah*, every act of *avodah*—every *mitzvah* performed with *kavanah* and *bitul*—carries the weight of the final refinement. We are not merely preparing for the *geulah*; we are actively bringing it into existence through our *avodah*.


## כ&quot;ח סיון

## 28 Sivan



**1.** The connection between the date of 28 Sivan and the theme of *hisgalus* (revelation) is well known. This is the day the Rebbe and the Rebbetzin arrived in the United States in 5701, an event that marked the beginning of the *hisgalus* of the Rebbe’s leadership and the subsequent dissemination of the wellsprings of Chassidus to the furthest reaches of the world.

**2.** In the *maamar* titled *Basi L’Gani* 5711, the Rebbe explains that the purpose of the *yiridah* (descent) of the *neshamah* into this world is to transform the world into a *dirah b’tachtonim*—a dwelling place for the *Ribono shel Olam* in the lowest realms. This is achieved specifically through the *avodah* of *is’hapcha* (transforming darkness into light), which is the essence of the *avodah* of the seventh generation.

**3.** The *hisgalus* of the Rebbe is not merely a historical event, but a continuous process of *avodah*. Just as the *hisgalus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* in the world requires the *keli* (vessel) of our *avodah*, so too the *hisgalus* of the *Nasi* requires the *hiskashrus* and *avodah* of *anash*. When a *chossid* engages in *avodah* with *bitul* and *mesiras nefesh*, he creates the *keli* for the *hisgalus* of the Rebbe’s *hashpa'ah* (influence) in his own life and in the world at large.

**4.** Therefore, the *avodah* of 28 Sivan is to internalize this *hisgalus*. It is not enough to commemorate the date; one must translate the *hisgalus* into a practical *avodah* of *hafatzas hamaayanos*. By strengthening our *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe and committing ourselves to the *avodah* of the seventh generation, we hasten the ultimate *hisgalus* of *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, when the *Ohr Ein Sof* will be revealed in this world in a complete and manifest way.

## פדיון שבויים

## Pidyon Shvuyim

 The concept of *pidyon shvuyim*—the redemption of captives—is a mitzvah that encompasses the entire essence of the Jewish soul. As our Sages state, "There is no greater mitzvah than *pidyon shvuyim*." This is not merely a quantitative statement regarding the importance of this mitzvah relative to others, but rather an expression of its qualitative nature: it touches upon the very core of *Klal Yisrael*.

Seemingly, one might ask: why is this mitzvah singled out as being so supreme? After all, the Torah contains many mitzvos that involve *mesiras nefesh* and profound *avodah*. Yet, when we examine the inner dimension of *pidyon shvuyim*, we understand that it is the ultimate expression of the bond between Hashem and the Jewish people. A *Yid* is never truly "captured" or separated from the source of holiness; even in the lowest depths of *galus*, the *neshamah* remains connected to the *Ein Sof*. The act of *pidyon shvuyim* is the external manifestation of this internal reality—it is the process of revealing that even that which appears to be in the domain of the "other" actually belongs to Hashem.

This is the deeper meaning behind the *avodah* of every *shaliach* and every *Chossid*. We are tasked with the "redemption" of the sparks of *Elokus* scattered throughout the world. By engaging in this *avodah* with *bitul* and *mesiras nefesh*, we not only liberate the captive, but we elevate the entire *seder hishtalshelus*, bringing the world closer to the ultimate *geulah*—the final *pidyon* of the entire Jewish people from the final *galus*.


## פורים

## Purim

 Regarding the laws of *mishloach manos* through a *shaliach*. Haman’s intention was not merely the destruction of the spiritual life of the Jewish people, etc.


## פטרבורג (עיר)

## Petersburg (City)

 The city of Petersburg is known as a place of *geulah* and liberation, for it was there that the Alter Rebbe was released from his imprisonment, and later, the Rayatz was also released from his imprisonment in that city. 

This is consistent with the general principle that the *avodah* of a Chossid is to transform the "Petersburg" of the world—the places of darkness and concealment—into a place of *geulah*. Through the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh* and *bitul*, one reveals that even in the most distant and concealed places, there is nothing but the light of Hashem. This is the essence of the *avodah* of *galus*: to transform the *galus* itself into *geulah*, until the ultimate *geulah* with Moshiach Tzidkeinu, when the light of Hashem will be revealed in all its glory, and the entire world will become a dwelling place for Him.

## פרד&quot;ס

## פשרות

## The Rejection of Compromise in Matters of Torah

The concept of compromise—*pesharah*—is a fundamental principle in the realm of interpersonal relations and civil law. The Gemara teaches that "a compromise is a mitzvah," as it fosters peace and harmony between parties. However, this applies exclusively to matters of civil litigation, where the objective is to reach an equitable settlement between two individuals.

When it comes to matters of Torah and mitzvos, however, the very notion of compromise is fundamentally misplaced. Torah is the expression of the Will of Hashem, which is absolute and immutable. One cannot "compromise" on the truth of Hashem or the integrity of His mitzvos, for doing so would imply that the Torah is subject to human negotiation or situational adjustment. In the realm of holiness, there is no middle ground, for any deviation from the precise path of the Torah is not a "compromise"—it is a departure from the truth itself.

Thus, while in the world of mundane affairs we seek to bridge gaps and find common ground, in the service of Hashem, our *avodah* is to stand firm in our commitment to the Torah’s demands, without dilution or concession. True peace—*shalom*—is not achieved by compromising the truth, but by elevating the world to the standard of the Torah, thereby revealing that the entire world is, in essence, a vessel for the light of Hashem.

## שלמה, רש&quot;י (כללים בפירושו)

## Shlomo, Rashi (Principles in his Commentary)

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="2"] It is not his custom to write the reasons for the mitzvos and the halachos without cause.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="13"] The emphasis on "the wine of Torah" is in his commentary on the Torah, as opposed to his commentary on the Shas.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="73"] In his commentary on the Torah, it is his custom to alter the language of Chazal in accordance with the *peshuto shel mikra*. Citing the name of the author of the statement in his commentary is intended to hint at an additional explanation, etc.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="76"] Principles regarding when he cites the Targum. The "Principles in the Words of Rashi" printed in many Chumashim require study as to who authored them.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="106"] Regarding textual variants in Rashi: sometimes the version that seems incomprehensible is the correct one.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="109"] Regarding the language of Rashi: "And the Midrash says, etc." — if his intent is to negate the simple interpretation.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="131"] His objective is to explain the *peshuto shel mikra* and not to copy the language of the Midrash.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="149"] In the parables and songs in the Torah, he also interprets according to the *drash*. Principles regarding his citation of the Targum.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="171"] If he sometimes interprets in one place according to one opinion and in a second place according to a different opinion.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="177"] When he brings two interpretations, it is because each of them contains a difficulty that is not present in the other, etc.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="178"] He brings Aggadah only if the words of Aggadah are necessary. Sometimes words that are part of his own commentary have been printed by mistake as a *dibbur hamaschil*.

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="181"] Regarding the language of Rashi: "And its Midrash in Aggadah."

[mafteach_gopage file="ls33" gopage="208"] He explains the reasons for the mitzvos only when it pertains to understanding the *peshat*.


## שלמי שמחה

## שלמי שמחה



The Gemara states that "one who is happy should bring a *korban* of *shelamim*." This is understood in the context of the *avodah* of a *chossid*: the *korban shelamim* represents the state of *shleimus* (wholeness/perfection) that results from *avodah*. 

Seemingly, one might ask: if a person has already reached a state of *shleimus* and happiness, why is there a need for a *korban*? A *korban* is a means of drawing closer to Hashem, typically necessitated by a lack or a need for elevation. Yet here, the *korban* is brought specifically *because* of the happiness and the *shleimus* that has already been attained.

But in truth, this is precisely the point. The *shleimus* of a *chossid* is not a static destination; it is a dynamic state of *ratzo v'shov*. The very happiness that one experiences—the *taanug* derived from one's *avodah*—must itself be brought as an offering to Hashem. By bringing the *korban shelamim*, the *chossid* acknowledges that his entire state of *shleimus* is not a personal acquisition, but a gift from the Ribono shel Olam. 

And with this we can understand the deeper significance of *simcha* in *avodah*. It is not merely an emotional byproduct; it is the vessel through which the *ohr* of the *mitzvah* is internalized. When the *simcha* is offered as a *korban*, it ceases to be a self-contained feeling and becomes a *dveikus*—a total *bitul* of the *nefesh* to the source of all *taanug*. This is the ultimate *shleimus*: that even in one's highest moments of joy, the *chossid* remains entirely bound to Hashem.

## שערות

## Hair Covering

[ftnref_ls33_263] Regarding the law of hair covering for a woman.

[ftnref_ls33_264] It is necessary that the entire head of a woman be covered. It is impossible that the fulfillment of Hashem’s mitzvah of hair covering would cause a headache or the like.

[ftnref_ls33_265] A distinction regarding hair covering with a wig versus a headscarf. It must be done immediately, without delay.

[ftnref_ls33_266] Rebuke and distress regarding the lack of hair covering for a woman.

[ftnref_ls33_268] Agreement to a shidduch is possible only when there is an agreement to conduct oneself according to the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, including hair covering, etc.

## תענית

## Ta'anis

 A postponed fast — its content and definition according to Halacha and according to Pnimiyus HaTorah. Two aspects of the four fasts: a day of favor for Hashem and a dimension of mourning. Their nullification and transformation into Yom Tov in the time to come. The vitality during the hunger of Yom Kippur extends also to the other fasts. The vitality on a fast day is from the level of "speaker" (medaber) which is above the levels of inanimate, vegetative, and animate (domem, tzomei'ach, chai). The nullification of the four fasts and their transformation into Yom Tov in the time to come.

## פסחים

## Pesach Sheini

## Horayos [A Sage Precedes a King of Yisrael]: [ftnref_ls33_42]


## משנה תורה

## Mishneh Torah

(From the general principles of the Rambam, that he does not write new laws). (His way is to take the simplest interpretation, even if it is not mentioned in the Gemara).

**In the Introduction**
All the mitzvos, etc., were given with their explanation, as it is said, "And I will give you..."

**The Counting of the Mitzvos**
Positive Mitzvah 159: To rest on the first day of the festival, as it is said, "And on the first day there shall be a holy convocation."
Positive Mitzvah 163: To rest on the first day of the seventh month, as it is said, "On the first of the month there shall be a Shabbaton for you."

**Laws of the Foundations of the Torah**
Chapter 1, Law 4: He alone is the Truth.
Chapter 2, Law 2: And this is the path to His love and fear, at the time when one contemplates, etc.

**Laws of Character Traits**
Chapter 3, Law 1: The Sages commanded, etc., is it not enough for you what the Torah has forbidden, etc.?
Chapter 3, Law 3: The Sages commanded and said, "And all your deeds shall be for the sake of Heaven," etc.
Chapter 4, Law 5: Leeks, onions, and garlic.

**Laws of Torah Study**
Chapter 3, Law 1: With three crowns, etc., for the crown of Torah is greater than both of them.
Chapter 3, Law 2: The Sages said, a mamzer who is a Torah scholar takes precedence over an ignorant Kohen Gadol, etc.

**Laws of Teshuvah**
Chapter 7, Law 1: A person should strive to do teshuvah, etc., for the life of the World to Come.
Chapter 7, Law 5: That Israel is destined to do teshuvah, etc.
Chapter 8, Law 2: [The ultimate reward for souls without bodies].
The righteous sit, etc., meaning, etc.
Chapter 8, Law 3: This is the reward, for there is no reward greater than this, etc.
Chapter 8, Law 6: That goodness, etc., "How great is Your goodness," etc.
Chapter 8, Law 7: To see the goodness of Hashem in the land of the living, etc.
Chapter 9, Law 1: And according to the greatness of his deeds and the abundance of his wisdom, he merits.
So that we may merit the life of the World to Come, etc.
Chapter 9, Law 2: And because of this they longed, etc., so that they would merit the life of the World to Come.
Chapter 10, Law 1: A person should not say, etc., that I will receive all the blessings, etc.
Chapter 10, Law 2: One who serves out of love, etc., does the truth because it is truth, etc., and not every wise man merits this.
Chapter 10, Law 3: And what is the love, etc., that he is obsessed with it always, etc.
Chapter 10, Law 4: So that I may be rich, etc., do not be like slaves, etc.
Chapter 10, Law 5: Therefore, when teaching the young, etc., this secret, little by little, etc.
Chapter 10, Law 6: For the love of the Ribono shel Olam is not bound, etc., until he is obsessed with it always, etc.

**Laws of Reading Shema**
Chapter 1, Law 2: They precede the reading of the Shema section, etc., and afterward the Tzitzis section, etc., as a remembrance of all the mitzvos.

**Laws of Prayer**
Chapter 8, Law 5: Ten, etc., a congregation, as it is said, "How long shall this evil congregation," etc.
Chapter 12, Law 11: And the translator does not lean, etc., he stands in awe and fear.
Chapter 13, Law 5: A simple custom, etc., and we read the Haftorah from the Merkabah.
Chapter 4, Law 10: [Tefillin are a sign].
Chapter 4, Law 25: As long as the Tefillin, etc., he is humble and G-d-fearing, etc.

**Laws of the Torah Scroll**
Chapter 10, Law 2: A kosher Torah scroll, one conducts oneself with it, etc., and great honor.
Chapter 10, Law 10: It is a mitzvah to designate a place for the Torah scroll, etc., the words that were in the Tablets of the Covenant, etc.
Chapter 10, Law 11: Anyone who sits before a Torah scroll should sit with gravity, etc.
At its end: And he shall honor it according to his strength, etc., and whoever honors the Torah, etc.

**Laws of Tzitzis**
Chapter 1, Law 1: That it is similar to the tzitzis of the head, etc.
Chapter 1, Law 8: And one must separate it until it is like the tzitzis of the hair of the head.
Chapter 3, Law 7: The obligation of tzitzis is by day, etc., "And you shall see it," etc.
Chapter 10, Law 8: Blessed, etc., who has bestowed goodness upon me.
Chapter 10, Law 9: Blessed, etc., who performed a miracle for me, etc.

**Laws of Yom Tov**
Chapter 1, Law 21: [Regarding the second day of Yom Tov in the Diaspora].
Chapter 6, Laws 17-18: And a person is obligated to be happy on them, etc., how, etc.
Chapter 6, Law 18: And when he eats and drinks, he is obligated to feed the convert, etc.
Chapter 6, Law 19: Even though eating and drinking on the festivals is included in the positive mitzvah, etc.
Chapter 7, Law 1: Since it is called a holy convocation, etc.

**Laws of Fasts**
Chapter 5, Law 1: To awaken the hearts to open the paths of teshuvah, etc.
Chapter 5, Law 4: The four fast days are explicitly mentioned in the Kabbalah: the fast of the fourth month, etc.
At its end: All these fasts are destined to be abolished, etc., and become days of celebration, etc.

**Laws of Marriage**
Chapter 3, Law 17: [Regarding the law that there is no agency for a non-Jew].
Chapter 5, Law 5: A Kohen who betrothed, etc., that they were not permitted, etc.

**Laws of Divorce**
Chapter 6, Law 9: In the Ra'avad: What are you, people of intelligence, etc., it is found, etc.
Chapter 7, Law 4: Even a hundred, etc., even though the first one died.
Chapter 7, Law 22: Even a hundred, etc.

**Laws of Forbidden Intercourse**
Chapter 13, Law 1: With three things did Israel enter the covenant, etc.
Chapter 13, Law 2: Circumcision was in Egypt, etc.
Chapter 13, Law 3: And immersion, etc., as it is said, "And you shall sanctify yourselves," etc.
Chapter 13, Law 6: Since the matter requires a Beis Din, one does not immerse him on Shabbos.
Chapter 14, Law 2: The fundamentals of the religion, etc., some of the mitzvos, etc.
Chapter 14, Law 8: He accepted upon himself the entire Torah except, etc.

**Laws of Oaths**
Chapter 1, Law 6: He swore, etc., that he would fast on Shabbos and Yom Tov, etc.
Chapter 6, Law 2: Thus they learned, etc., "He shall not profane his word," etc.

**Laws of Vows**
Chapter 13, Law 2: In the Kesef Mishneh: The Sage rules that the vow did not take effect from the outset, etc.
Chapter 13, Laws 23-24: One who makes vows, etc., he is diligent and praiseworthy, etc., he should not multiply, etc.

**Laws of Terumah**
Beginning of Chapter 4: [Regarding the law that there is no agency for a non-Jew].
Beginning of Chapter 5: One only separates Terumah from the finest, etc.

**Laws of First Fruits**
Chapter 3, Law 12: At its end.

**Laws of Shemitah and Yovel**
At its end: He was set apart to serve Hashem, etc., "Your judgments will teach," etc., every single person, etc.

**Laws of the Vessels of the Sanctuary**
Chapter 5, Law 7: The Kohen Gadol, etc., his home is in Jerusalem and he does not move from there.
Chapter 6, Law 9: In the Mishneh Lamelech regarding the matter of handing it over to the public properly.

**Laws of Forbidden Sacrifices**
Chapter 7, Law 1: He shall not bring a lean or ugly lamb.
At its end: The finest, etc., and the average, and the inferior.
And he shall bring his offering from the finest, etc., and the same applies to everything, etc.

**Laws of the Holy Temple**
Chapter 14, Law 14: In the Lechem Mishneh regarding the obligation of women in the joy of Yom Tov.

**Laws of the Passover Offering**
Chapter 4, Law 1: And not all of Israel dies.

**Laws of the Korban Pesach**
Chapter 5, Law 1: The second Pesach... is a separate festival.

**Laws of Chagigah**
Chapter 1, Law 1: And the joy mentioned regarding the festivals is, etc.
The peace-offerings of the joy of Chagigah.
Women are obligated in this mitzvah.
Chapter 2, Law 10: Israel fulfills their obligation of the peace-offerings of joy through vows and voluntary offerings, etc.

**Laws of the Red Heifer**
Chapter 2, Law 6: And if there was nothing there but the ashes of one heifer, etc.
End of Chapter 3: And nine red heifers were made, etc., and the tenth will be made by Melech HaMashiach.

**Laws of Tzaraas**
Chapter 15, Law 4: Both of them uncover, etc.
At its end: It was a sign and a wonder in Israel.

**Laws of Rebels**
Chapter 2: [Regarding customs].

**Laws of Kings**
Chapter 3, Law 6: For his heart is the heart of the entire congregation of Israel.
Chapter 8, Law 10: And so he commanded, etc., to coerce all the inhabitants of the world, etc.
Beginning of Chapter 11: All the laws return, etc., they offer sacrifices, etc.
End of Chapter 11: He will fix the entire world to serve Hashem together, etc., with one shoulder.
Chapter 12, Law 4: The Sages longed, etc., so that they would be free, etc.
At its end: And in that time, etc., and no jealousy or competition.
